▬●●▬

890

The Ruthenian Recension
History
The “Liturgical Books according to the Ruthenian
Recension for Ukrainians and Ruthenians” (Libri Liturgici
Recensio Ruthena pro Ucrainis et Ruthenis) are typical
editions of the liturgical books published by the Sacred
Congregation for the Eastern Churches of the Holy See
of Rome. They were issued from 1940 to 1975 in Church
Slavonic according to the liturgical practices of the historic
Metropolitanate of Kiev and the Churches sui iuris, and
eparchies formed from the historic Eparchy of Mukačevo. The
Holy See of Rome issued these texts in response to the request
of the Ukrainian and Ruthenian Catholic bishops following
their meeting in 1932. This volume is an English translation
of the Часословъ (Časoslov). The Sacred Congregation for
the Eastern Churches published the Book of Hours in two
editions in 1950, the regular edition as translated here, and an
expanded edition which appeared in the form of a Великий
Часословъ (Velikyj Časoslov) or Great Book of Hours
which included additional material: the Inter-hours and the
Panaghia, the Common Служба (Služba) for feasts and prefeasts of Christ and the Common Служба (Služba) for feasts
of the Theotokos, the Canon to the Guardian Angel, a Canon
of Repentance in Tone Six to the Most Holy Theotokos, the
Служба (Služba) for the Departed for Friday evening and
891

The Book of Hours: Časoslov

Saturday morning, a Common Служба (Služba) for all days
to our Lord Jesus Christ, the texts of the Eleven Resurrection
Gospels of Sunday Matins with the eleven Exapostilaria and
the Gospel stichera, a Typica for the Sunday of Pascha, a
synaxarion for each day in the Menologion as well as fasting
regulations, the Order of the Canon and Prayers before the
reception of Holy Communion and the Thanksgiving Prayers
after the reception of Holy Communion, and an alphabetical
index of saints. This larger version of the Часословъ expanded
the contents of Daily Matins with the addition of the complete
texts of the eight Old Testament scriptural canticles and the
New Testament canticle of Zechariah along with the canticle
of the Theotokos. There were also other differences: the
Midnight Hymn to the Theotokos which was presented at
the conclusion of Morning Prayer in the smaller volume, was
omitted in the larger one. The larger Часословъ (Časoslov)
also omitted the Canon of the Hodegetria Mother of God.
The Common Служба (Služba) to the Archangels and Angels
commonly sung on Mondays, presented a different collection
of stichera at Psalm 140 of Vespers and an alternate Canon to
the Bodiless Ones in place of the Canon to the Archangels in
the smaller Часословъ.
The only previous attempt to issue a Book of Hours in
English according to the typical edition of the Ruthenian
Recension was the Horologion, Volume 1, 1967 and
Horologion: The Days of Lent and Life Volume 2, 1968.
These were produced by the Byzantine Franciscan Friars of
Holy Protection Monastery, New Canaan, Connecticut, with
the blessing of the Custos of Saint Mary of the Angels. These
volumes were mostly complete, omitting daily Morning
and Evening Prayers and with several other lacunae. The
translation was their own, primarily the work of the Friars
Marion Francis Kowala and George Appleyard, and they
892

The Ruthenian Recension

used the psalms from the Jerusalem Bible. Another attempt
to produce an English language translation of the Часословъ
was part of an initiative of Bishop Milan Šašik, C.M., Bishop
of Mukačevo. On May 30, 2013 (Protocol No. 086/13),
Bishop Šašik had enlisted the services of Jack Figel and
Eastern Christian Publications to produce parallel EnglishChurch Slavonic study editions of the collection of liturgical
books published by the Sacred Congregation of the Eastern
Churches according to the Ruthenian Recension. The first
section of the Великий Часословъ (Velikyj Časoslov) 1950,
with an English translation facing each Church Slavonic page,
was published in 2017.

This Edition
This present volume uses existing translations from
the revised translations promulgated by the Metropolitan
Archbishop and Bishops of the Byzantine Ruthenian
Metropolitan Church of Pittsburgh on January 6, 2007,
and any subsequent official texts. These translations were
revisions of previously issued texts according to the Ruthenian
Recension which received approbation of the Metropolitan
Archbishop or an eparchial bishop of the Byzantine Ruthenian
Metropolitan Church of Pittsburgh. These texts were based
on the translation style of the seminal text approved by the
Holy See December 10, 1964, The Divine Liturgy of our
Father among the Saints John Chrysostom published by the
Byzantine Liturgical Conference 1965 with the blessing of
the eparchial bishops of Pittsburgh and Passaic. That text,
in turn, followed the arrangement and layout of the typical
edition of that liturgy issued in 1941 by the Congregation of
the Eastern Churches with the exception of the psalms. For
the psalms for the 2007 revision, the Inter-eparchial Liturgical
893

The Book of Hours: Časoslov

Commission of the Byzantine Ruthenian Metropolitan Church
of Pittsburgh chose to use The Psalms— A New Translation,
The Grail, 1963. Therefore, the Grail Psalms are used in this
volume and are printed in verse as printed in the Grail texts.
In the typical editions of the Ruthenian Recension in Church
Slavonic from the Congregation of the Eastern Churches the
psalms are set in paragraph form. The psalms are the inspired
Word of God given to us to use as the words of our prayer to
God, so it is presented in verse to facilitate our prayer, but
also the psalms are God’s Word to us. The latter function
is as a reading from the Sacred Scripture for each horarium
of prayer and to facilitate this function it is understandable
they would be printed in paragraph form. Texts that had been
used unofficially in the Ruthenian Church and had become
popularized, but which were not in accord with the Church
Slavonic texts, were reworked. The troparia and kontakia for
the Menologion which did not appear in official texts have
been newly translated from the Church Slavonic.
The prayers at the conclusion of each Служба (Služba) for
every day of the week in the Canonicon have never appeared
in English. These required a fresh translation and appear in
this volume for the first time in English.
In this present volume, the capitalization style of the 1965
translation and subsequent translations are used for pronouns
referring to the Godhead. This style seemed more respectful,
and it is easier when praying to quickly understand to whom
the pronouns refer: God, the Theotokos or a saint. In accord
with the 2007 revision texts, Bohorodica has been translated as
Theotokos while Mati Boža has been translated as Mother of
God. In addition, the typical edition usually uses the vocative
form of the title father, Отчє, when inviting the celebrating
priest to bless. However, there are also instances in which
894

The Ruthenian Recension

Master, Владыко, is used and these are specified in the text.  
This English language translation of the Часословъ
(Časoslov) follows the pattern established in the typical edition
regarding the red-letter incipit at the beginning of psalms,
the priestly prayers, and the initial sticheron of the weekday
services of the Canonicon, the Service to Archangels and
Angels. Additionally, the Church Slavonic edition also uses
a red-letter incipit for certain psalm verses of the Polyeleos
of Sunday and Festal Matins and also for the First Kathisma
at Vespers. Its usage in those places is to indicate how those
psalms may be abbreviated, such that only the verse beginning
with the red-letter incipit may be chanted in the abbreviated
form.
It should be noted that the typical edition of the Часословъ
(Časoslov) varies in the usage of the prayers commonly called
the “Usual Beginning Prayers,” Начало Обычноє (Načalo
obyčnoje). In some cases, they are presented completely,
while in other places the prayers are only referenced in
abbreviated form in the rubrics, prescribing that the prayers
be prayed in full. In yet other cases, the order of prayer begins
with the invitatory, “Come, let us worship” such as for the
First Hour. In the latter instance, the Часословъ (Časoslov)
expects that the First Hour would follow immediately at the
completion of Matins and thus the Usual Beginning Prayers
would be omitted. However, if the First Hour is prayed
separately instead of immediately following Matins, the Usual
Beginning Prayers should be prayed in their entirety. Another
variation is seen in Parakleisis, where the rubric indicates that
following the priestly blessing, “Blessed is our God,” Psalm
142 is prayed, yet the Usual Beginning Prayers are expected
to be prayed before Psalm 142.
When a translation of a typical edition is made to a
vernacular, the formatting of the text must be made in accord
895

The Book of Hours: Časoslov

with the original. This is faithfully observed here, with
the exception of the psalms as mentioned above, and the
following other exceptions. Additional words in the rubrics,
titles of prayers, or other notes which appear in other editions,
or are intended to help or clarify this current edition, are in
brackets. Prayers such as texts for recent beatifications or
commemorations observed only in the United States which
do not appear in the Ruthenian Recension of the Часословъ
(Časoslov) are enclosed in brackets. For any prayer that is a
complete quotation from Sacred Scripture or where an entire
verse is a scriptural text, the reference appears in brackets.
Scriptural quotations embedded within the texts of prayers,
canons, stichera, troparia and kontakia and not indicated.
As expected, the typical edition of the Часословъ
(Časoslov) does not have detailed rubrics for the priestcelebrant. These are found exactly where one would expect,
the Лїтурґїконъ сїєсть Служєбникъ (Liturgikon sijest’
Služebnik), Rome, 1952. In that volume are found the rubrics
for the priest-celebrant for all the services of the Divine
Office, including the special forms of Vespers and Matins for
the Great Fast, Great and Holy Week, and Pascha. Indications
for Sunday and Festal Matins and Vespers which allow for
the ministry of a deacon are also included. Another source for
rubrics, specifically for Sunday and Festal Vespers and Matins,
are found in the Ordo Celebrationis, Rome, 1944 (English
and Latin/English editions by Eastern Christian Publications,
1996 and 2007).
The headers, artwork and icon engravings are from the
larger edition of the Часословъ (Časoslov), Rome, 1950.
